## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillator dynamics (ODEs / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard form of second-order oscillator equations (linear, damped, driven, and nonlinear such as Duffing or van der Pol). Typical structures combine restoring forces in x, dissipation terms in v, and external/parametric forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Undamped linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (conservative spring-like restoring acceleration)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped oscillator with drag proportional to velocity)
- Frequency-shifted linear oscillator (explicit offset): dv_dt = c0 * (x + c1) + c2 * v (equilibrium shifted by preload/gravity)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (nonlinear stiffness plus linear dissipation)
- Soft saturation in restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * tanh(c1 * x) + c2 * v (bounded restoring force / actuator saturation)
- Pendulum-type restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (angular oscillator where sin term replaces linear x)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag proportional to speed squared)
- Nonlinear damping polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent dissipation beyond viscous)
- van der Pol oscillator form: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillator / limit cycles via negative damping at small x)
- Rayleigh oscillator form: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (self-excitation controlled by velocity-dependent damping)
- Driven oscillator (additive forcing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance/chaos regimes)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)
- Potential-derived conservative force (generic): dv_dt = -c0 * d_dx( c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**4 ) (acceleration from a polynomial potential; expands to linear+cubic terms in x)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends primarily on x (often odd in x), with little/no dependence on v or t; indicates acceleration from a potential energy gradient.
- Linear damping signature: additive term proportional to v; produces spiral decay in phase space and monotone energy loss.
- Nonlinear (amplitude-dependent) stiffness: presence of x**3 or higher odd powers; implies frequency depends on oscillation amplitude (hardening/softening).
- Self-excitation / limit-cycle signature: damping coefficient changes sign with state, e.g., (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v; yields growth at small amplitude and saturation at large amplitude.
- External periodic driving: additive sin/cos terms in t; generates forced response and resonance peaks when drive frequency matches natural frequency.
- Parametric resonance indicator: x multiplied by a periodic function of t, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x; can destabilize the trivial equilibrium even without additive forcing.
- Coulomb-like dry friction approximation: dv_dt includes -c0 * sign(v) (often approximated by -c0 * tanh(c1*v)); creates stick–slip and nonsmooth dynamics.
- Geometric/pendulum nonlinearity: sin(c*x) restoring term; reduces to linear for small x but strongly nonlinear near large angles, causing period elongation.
- Quadratic drag behavior: v*Abs(v) term; dissipation grows rapidly with speed and produces non-exponential amplitude decay.
- Symmetry cue: if the physics is symmetric under x→-x, v→-v, dv_dt typically uses odd functions of x and odd functions of v (e.g., x, x**3, v, v**3), with even-in-state terms suggesting bias or external fields.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO17)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v - c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):  
\[
f(x,t,v)=0.4607662803\sin(t)\;-\;0.2634379499\,v\sin(x)\;-\;0.5268758999\,v\;-\;2.5071295689\,x
\]
Key required structures:
- a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (no other \(t\)-dependence),
- a linear \(-2.5071\,x\) term,
- a linear-in-\(v\) term \(-0.5269\,v\),
- and crucially a **product** term \(v\sin(x)\) with coefficient \(-0.2634\).
No other dependence (no constants, no \(v^k\), no \(x^k\), no rational \(v/(x+\cdot)^3\), etc.).

Now check candidates.

**Candidates 1–40, 42–49:**  
All of these have only combinations of:
- \(x\) terms (possibly multiple linear \(x\) terms),
- \(\sin(\text{affine in }t)\) (good for matching \(\sin(t)\) via phase/frequency choices),
- polynomial-in-\(v\) terms (like \(v, v^3, v^4, v^5\)),
- rational terms \(v/(c+x)^3\),
- extra constants, \(x^3, x^5\), \(x^c\), \(x\cdot(c+v)^2\), etc.

None of these candidates contains any term of the form \(v\sin(x)\) (a multiplicative coupling between \(v\) and a trig function of \(x\)). Because \(x\) and \(v\) are independent variables and can take negative values, you cannot “fake” \(v\sin(x)\) using:
- a linear \(v\) term plus an \(x\)-only term,
- a rational \(v/(c+x)^3\) term,
- or any polynomial in \(v\) alone.
So **all candidates 1–40 and 42–49 fail** due to the missing \(v\sin(x)\) structure (even though many could match the \(\sin(t)\), \(x\), and \(v\) linear parts by setting some coefficients to zero and tuning others).

Now the only candidates that even include \(\sin(\text{affine in }x)\) are 41, 46, 50 (and 44 has \(\sin(\text{affine in }v)\), which is not useful).

---

### Candidate 41
\[
c0x + c1\sin(c2+c3t) + c4\sin(c5x+c6) + c7v + c8\frac{v}{(c9+x)^3}
\]
- Has \(\sin(\cdot x)\) but it is **not multiplied by \(v\)**; it’s an \(x\)-only trig term.
- The only \(v\)-dependence is \(c7v\) and \(c8 v/(c9+x)^3\). Neither can produce \(v\sin(x)\) for all \(x\).
- If you set \(c8=0\), you still cannot create \(v\sin(x)\). If you keep \(c8\neq 0\), you introduce a rational dependence on \(x\) not present in GT.
So **cannot match**.

### Candidate 44
\[
c0x + c1\sin(c2+c3t) + c4\sin(c5v+c6) + c7v + c8\frac{v}{(c9+x)^3} + v
\]
- Introduces \(\sin(\text{affine in }v)\), which GT does not have.
- Still no \(v\sin(x)\).
So **cannot match**.

### Candidate 46
\[
c0x + c1\sin(c2+c3t) + c4\sin(c5x+c6) + c7v + \frac{v}{(c8+x)^3}
\]
- Same fundamental issue as 41: \(\sin(\cdot x)\) is not multiplied by \(v\).
- The rational \(v/(c8+x)^3\) cannot equal \(-0.2634\,v\sin(x)\) for all \(x\) (different functional form; also would have poles).
So **cannot match**.

### Candidate 50
\[
c0 + c1\sin(c2+c3t) + c4\sin(c5x+c6) + c7v + \frac{v}{(c8+x)^3}
\]
- Again no \(v\sin(x)\).
- Also has an additive constant \(c0\) which GT lacks (could set \(c0=0\), but still missing \(v\sin(x)\)).
So **cannot match**.

---

### Trig phase/frequency note
Many candidates have \(c1\sin(c2+c3t)\), which *could* match \(0.460766\sin(t)\) by setting \(c3=1\), \(c2=0\) (or any \(2\pi k\)), \(c1=0.460766\). That part is not the blocker. The blocker is the indispensable coupling term \(-0.2634379499\,v\sin(x)\), which no candidate can generate because none contains a product of \(v\) with a trig function of \(x\).

**Conclusion:** No candidate can be made exactly equal to the GT for all real \(x,t,v\).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO17)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v - c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: -2.50713*x + 0.46077*sin(t) - 0.26344*v*sin(x) - 0.52688*v**

The key terms are:
1. A linear term in x
2. sin(t) 
3. **v*sin(x)** - a product of v and sin(x)
4. A linear term in v

The critical term is **-β*sin(x)*v** = -0.26344*v*sin(x). This is a nonlinear coupling between v and sin(x).

Let me examine what basis functions each candidate offers and whether any can produce a v*sin(x) term.

Most candidates have the structure: `c0*x + c1*sin(c2 + c3*t) + [extra terms] + [v terms] + [v/(c+x)^3 terms]`

The key question: Can `v/(c+x)^3` approximate `-β*v*sin(x)` exactly? No - `v/(c+x)^3` is a rational function of x times v, while `v*sin(x)` involves a transcendental function. These are fundamentally different basis functions and cannot be exactly equal for all x.

Similarly, terms like `x*(c+v)^2`, `x^3`, `v^3`, `v^4`, `v^5`, `x^5`, `log(...)`, `exp(...)`, `x^c` cannot produce v*sin(x).

**Candidate 41**: `c0*x + c1*sin(c2+c3*t) + c4*sin(c5*x+c6) + c7*v + c8*v/(c9+x)^3`
This has sin(c5*x+c6) but NOT multiplied by v. It's just an additive sin(x) term, not v*sin(x). Cannot match.

**Candidate 44**: `c0*x + c1*sin(c2+c3*t) + c4*sin(c5*v+c6) + c7*v + c8*v/(c9+x)^3 + v`
Has sin(c5*v+c6), not v*sin(x). Cannot match.

**Candidate 46**: `c0*x + c1*sin(c2+c3*t) + c4*sin(c5*x+c6) + c7*v + v/(c8+x)^3`
Same issue - sin(x) not multiplied by v. Cannot match.

**Candidate 50**: `c0 + c1*sin(c2+c3*t) + c4*sin(c5*x+c6) + c7*v + v/(c8+x)^3`
Same - no v*sin(x) term.

**Candidate 47**: `c0*x + c1*sin(c2+c3*t) + c4*log(c5*v+1) + c6*x^c7 + c8*v + v/(c9+x)^3`
No v*sin(x) term.

None of the candidates contain a term of the form `v*sin(x)` (or equivalently `v*cos(x)` with phase shift). The GT requires this specific basis function, and by the principle of linear independence of basis functions (polynomials, rational functions, and transcendental functions like sin(x) are linearly independent), no combination of the offered terms can exactly reproduce v*sin(x).

Every candidate lacks the essential v*sin(x) coupling term. None can match.
